       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The <b>United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland</b> or simply the <b>United Kingdom</b> (<b>UK</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>. It is a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> that is made up of <a href="/wiki/Countries_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Countries of the United Kingdom">four separate countries</a>: <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>. It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a>, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> and the <a href="/wiki/G8" title="G8">G8</a>. It had the sixth largest economy in the world by <a href="/wiki/Nominal_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="Nominal GDP">nominal GDP</a> in 2019. </p>
      <p>Around 66 million people live in the UK (2018).<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[13]</a></sup> They can be divided into four big <a href="/wiki/Nationality" title="Nationality">nationalities</a> based on the countries where they live (or where they were born or their <a href="/wiki/Ancestry" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancestry">ancestry</a>). </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> is the biggest country, where most people in the UK live. People who live in England are called <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English</a>. Their native <a href="/wiki/Language" title="***REMOVED***">language</a> is called <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, which is spoken by almost everyone in England. A few people in <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>, a county of England, can speak <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Celtic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Celtic language">Celtic language</a>.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, north of England, is the second biggest country. People who live here are called <a href="/wiki/Scottish_people" title="Scottish people">Scottish</a>, and a Scottish person may be called a Scot. Some speak languages other than English: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a>, a Celtic language, or <a href="/wiki/Scots" title="Scots">Scots</a>, which is a lot like English.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> is to the west of England. Its people are called <a href="/wiki/Welsh_people" title="Welsh people">Welsh</a> and they have their own Celtic language which is also called <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a>. Not everyone in Wales can speak Welsh, but almost everyone can speak English.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> is the smallest country. Unlike the other three countries, it is not on the island of <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a>: it is part of the island called <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>. Northern Ireland takes up about a sixth of Ireland (with the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> taking up the remainder). People who live in Northern Ireland are either Irish, British, or Northern Irish; it is their choice what they want to be identified as and they can choose British or Irish <a href="/wiki/Nationality" title="Nationality">nationality</a> (or both). The people who live there usually speak English, but some people speak <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Scots_dialects" title="Ulster Scots dialects">Ulster Scots</a>, which is similar to Scots spoken in Scotland.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>The UK has many <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">cities</a>. England is home to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, the biggest city in the UK and also its <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital city</a>. There are also many other big cities in England including <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle upon Tyne</a>. Scotland has the big cities of <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swansea" title="Swansea">Swansea</a> are in Wales and <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a> is in Northern Ireland. </p>
      <p>Between the 17th and mid 20th-centuries, Britain was a world power. It became a <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">colonial empire</a> that controlled large areas of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[14]</a></sup> At its height in 1922, more than 458 million people lived in the British Empire, one-fifth of the Earth's population. Its area was 13,012,000 square miles: almost a quarter of the Earth's land area. The empire was sometimes called 'the empire on which the sun never sets', which describes a large empire where the sun is always shining on at least one of its territories. Almost all countries left and became independent from the empire in the 20th century, although Britain keeps <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">links with most countries of its former empire</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=1" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Prehistory">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Change section: Prehistory">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Stonehenge_Wide_Angle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Stonehenge_Wide_Angle.jpg/250px-Stonehenge_Wide_Angle.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Stonehenge_Wide_Angle.jpg/375px-Stonehenge_Wide_Angle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Stonehenge_Wide_Angle.jpg/500px-Stonehenge_Wide_Angle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stonehenge_Wide_Angle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Stonehenge" title="Stonehenge">Stonehenge</a> in the United Kingdom
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">Archaeological</a> remains show that the first group of modern people to live in the British Isles were hunter-gatherers after the last <a href="/wiki/Ice_age" title="Ice age">ice age</a> ended.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[15]</a></sup> The date is not known: perhaps as early as 8000<small>BC</small> but certainly by 5000<small>BC</small>. They built <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">mesolithic</a> wood and stone <a href="/wiki/Monument" title="Monument">monuments</a>. <a href="/wiki/Stonehenge" title="Stonehenge">Stonehenge</a> was built between 3000 and 1600<small>BC</small>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[16]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Celt" class="mw-redirect" title="Celt">Celtic</a> tribes arrived from mainland Europe. Britain was a changing collection of tribal areas, with no overall leader. Julius Caesar tried to invade (take over) the island in 55<small>BC</small> but was not able to do so. The Romans successfully invaded in 43<small>AD</small>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[17]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=2" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: History">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Change section: History">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="History of the United Kingdom">History of the United Kingdom</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Written history began in Britain when writing was brought to Britain by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a>. Rome ruled in Britain from 44AD to 410AD, but they only ruled England and Wales. The Romans never ruled Scotland north of the Clyde-Forth valley, or Ireland; their northern boundary varied from time to time, and was marked for a while at <a href="/wiki/Hadrian%27s_Wall" title="Hadrian's Wall">Hadrian's Wall</a>. </p>
      <p>After the Romans, two waves of <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigrants</a> came to Britain. The first were <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">German</a> tribes: the <a href="/wiki/Angles" title="Angles">Angles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jutes" title="Jutes">Jutes</a>. <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, the language, is a development from <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Saxon">Anglo-Saxon</a> <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a>, and is a Germanic language. The second were the <a href="/wiki/Viking" class="mw-redirect" title="Viking">Vikings</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Britain_unified">Britain unified</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=3" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Britain unified">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Change section: Britain unified">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>After a long period when <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> was split into various kingdoms, it was made into one country by Æthelstan (<a href="/wiki/Athelstan" title="Athelstan">Athelstan</a>) in 945<small>AD</small>. England and Wales were unified by <a href="/wiki/Edward_I_of_England" title="Edward I of England">Edward I</a> (Longshanks) by force in the 13th century. </p>
      <p>Union with Scotland took much longer; there were hundreds of years of conflicts between both parts of Britain. This union between England and Scotland in 1707 formed the United Kingdom of Great Britain, which merged Scotland and England into one country. </p>
      <p>In 1603, when <a href="/wiki/Queen" title="Queen">Queen</a> <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth I of England">Elizabeth I of England</a> died, her closest relative was <a href="/wiki/King" title="King">King</a> <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_England" title="James I of England">James VI of Scotland</a>. He became king of England as well as king of Scotland. In 1707, the Scottish and English Parliaments agreed the Treaty of Union, which joined the two countries into one country called <i>The Kingdom of Great Britain</i> under Queen <a href="/wiki/Anne_of_Great_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="Anne of Great Britain">Anne</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Queen_Elizabeth_II_March_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Queen_Elizabeth_II_March_2015.jpg/180px-Queen_Elizabeth_II_March_2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Queen_Elizabeth_II_March_2015.jpg/270px-Queen_Elizabeth_II_March_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Queen_Elizabeth_II_March_2015.jpg/360px-Queen_Elizabeth_II_March_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1820" data-file-height="2400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Queen_Elizabeth_II_March_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth</a> has reigned since 1952.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>By 1800, both Scotland and England had already independently had much influence over <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> since 1200. In that year laws were passed in Great Britain and Ireland to merge the two states. The new country was called the <i>United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland</i>. In 1922 much of Ireland became independent as the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a> (now called <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a>) from the United Kingdom. However, six northern counties (called <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>) continue to be part of the United Kingdom. The country was renamed <i>The United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland</i>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parliament">Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=4" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Parliament">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Change section: Parliament">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The British people are represented by members of <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">Parliament</a>, not ruled by monarchs. After the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell" title="Oliver Cromwell">Oliver Cromwell</a> became Lord Protector, and the monarchy was disbanded. Although the monarchy was restored after his death, the Crown slowly became the secondary power, and Parliament the first. Members of Parliament (called MPs) were elected, but until the early twentieth century, only men who owned property could vote. In the nineteenth century, more people were given <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">suffrage</a> (the right to vote), but even so, by 1900, women could not vote, and only 40% of men were rich enough to vote. But in 1928, all men and women got the vote: this is called universal suffrage. </p>
      <p>Parliament is in <a href="/wiki/Westminster" title="Westminster">Westminster</a> in London, but it has power over the whole of the UK. Wales, Scotland and Northern Ireland now each have their own parliaments but they have more limited powers. Scotland has the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a> at Holyrood. Wales has the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales" title="National Assembly for Wales">National Assembly for Wales</a> in Cardiff and the Northern Ireland has the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly" title="Northern Ireland Assembly">Northern Ireland Assembly</a> at Stormont. England does not have a separate parliament. There are also parliaments in the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">Guernsey</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a>, which are all independent island states for which the UK has <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependencies" title="Crown dependencies">some responsibility</a> in international law. </p>
      <p>Almost all members of Parliament belong to <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">political parties</a>. The biggest parties are the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservative Party">Conservative Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Labour Party">Labour Party</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats" title="Liberal Democrats">Liberal Democrats</a>. Members of the same party agree to act and vote more or less together. A party with more than half the seats (a majority) forms the government; the leader of the party becomes the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister">Prime Minister</a>, who then appoints other ministers. Because the government has a majority in Parliament, it can normally control what laws are passed. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Native_languages_in_the_UK">Native languages in the UK</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=5" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Native languages in the UK">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Change section: Native languages in the UK">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Celtic_languages">Celtic languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=6" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Celtic languages">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Change section: Celtic languages">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish Gaelic</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germanic_languages">Germanic languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=7" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Germanic languages">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Change section: Germanic languages">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Scots" title="Scots">Scots</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ulster_Scots" class="mw-redirect" title="Ulster Scots">Ulster Scots</a></li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_languages">Foreign languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=8" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Foreign languages">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Change section: Foreign languages">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Major languages spoken in the United Kingdom other than English include <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a> (500,000 approximate number of speakers in the United Kingdom), Eastern Panjabi or <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_language" title="Punjabi language">Punjabi</a> (471,000), <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a> (400,000), <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a> (400,000), <a href="/wiki/Cantonese_language" title="Cantonese language">Cantonese</a> (300,000), <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> (200,000), Southwestern Caribbean <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">Creole</a> English (170,000).<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[18]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=9" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Geography">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Change section: Geography">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="box-No_sources plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation">

        <div class="thumbcaption">

          <a href="/wiki/File:Uk_topo_en.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The topography of the UK
        </div>

      <p>The UK is made up of four different countries: <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>. The capital city of Wales is <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>. The capital city of England is <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>. The capital city of Scotland is <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> and the capital city of Northern Ireland is <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>. Other large cities in the UK are <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool,_Mersyside" class="mw-redirect" title="Liverpool, Mersyside">Liverpool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle upon Tyne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southampton" title="Southampton">Southampton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leicester" title="Leicester">Leicester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coventry" title="Coventry">Coventry</a>, <a href="/wiki/City_of_Bradford" title="City of Bradford">Bradford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nottingham" title="Nottingham">Nottingham</a>. </p>
      <p>The UK is north-west off the coast of mainland <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>. Around the UK are the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>. The UK also rules, usually indirectly, a number of smaller places (mostly islands) round the world, which are known as <i>overseas territories</i>. They are remnants of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Weather" title="Weather">weather</a> of the United Kingdom is changeable and unpredictable. Summers are moderately warm, winters are cool to cold. Rain falls throughout the year, and more on the west than the east because of its northerly latitude and the warm water from the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" class="mw-redirect" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>. The usually moderate prevailing winds from the Atlantic may be interrupted by <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> air from the north-east or hot air from the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=10" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Politics">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Change section: Politics">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="box-No_sources plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">

        <div class="thumbcaption">

          <a href="/wiki/File:Boris_Johnson_official_portrait_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The current <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister of the United Kingdom</a> is <a href="/wiki/Boris_Johnson" title="Boris Johnson">Boris Johnson</a> since 2019
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The UK is a <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> based on a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hereditary_monarchy" title="Hereditary monarchy">hereditary monarchy</a>. The people of the United Kingdom vote for a <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">members of Parliament</a> to speak for them and to make laws for them. Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Monarch" title="Monarch">queen</a> of the UK and is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>. Even though she is the head of state, she does not actually govern the country. The <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">government</a>, led by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister">Prime Minister</a>, governs the country and decides <a href="/wiki/Policy" class="mw-disambig" title="Policy">policy</a>. Today, the Prime Minister is <a href="/wiki/Boris_Johnson" title="Boris Johnson">Boris Johnson</a>, who is the leader of the Conservative Party. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">Parliament</a> is where laws are made. It has three parts: the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a>, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a>, and the Queen. The House of Commons is the most powerful part. It is where Members of Parliament sit. The Prime Minister sits here as well, because they are a Member of Parliament. The people who sit in the House of Lords are called peers: they are not chosen by the people. Most peers are now appointed by the government. There are some who are hereditary <a href="/wiki/Peerage" title="Peerage">peers</a> (their fathers were peers); and a few others, such as certain <a href="/wiki/Bishop" title="Bishop">bishops</a> in the established <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">Judiciary</a> (Law Lords). </p>
      <p>Scotland has its own devolved Parliament with power to make laws on things like education, health and Scottish law. Northern Ireland and Wales have their own devolved Assemblies which have some powers but less than the Scottish parliament. The UK Parliament remains sovereign and it could end the devolved administrations at any time. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=11" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Military">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Change section: Military">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="box-No_sources plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-4.svg" class="image"><img alt="Question book-4.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Question_book-4.svg/50px-Question_book-4.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Question_book-4.svg/75px-Question_book-4.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Question_book-4.svg/100px-Question_book-4.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="262" data-file-height="204"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>does not have any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> You can help Wikipedia by finding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:RELIABLE" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:RELIABLE">good</a> sources, and adding them.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2020</span>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The UK has a military of around 223,000 people, not including reserve forces. The UK has one of the most advanced militaries in the world, alongside such countries such as the <a href="/wiki/USA" class="mw-redirect" title="USA">USA</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, and operates a large army (<a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a>), a sizable navy (<a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>) and air force (<a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a>). From the 18th century to the early 20th century, the UK was one of the most powerful nations in the world, with a huge navy (due to the fact it was surrounded by sea, so a large navy was the most practical option). This status has faded in recent times, but the UK remains a member of various military groups such as the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">UN Security Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>. It is also still seen as a great military power. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=12" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Economy">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Change section: Economy">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="box-No_sources plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-4.svg" class="image"><img alt="Question book-4.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Question_book-4.svg/50px-Question_book-4.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Question_book-4.svg/75px-Question_book-4.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Question_book-4.svg/100px-Question_book-4.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="262" data-file-height="204"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>does not have any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> You can help Wikipedia by finding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:RELIABLE" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:RELIABLE">good</a> sources, and adding them.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2020</span>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The UK is a <a href="/wiki/Development" class="mw-disambig" title="Development">developed</a> country with the sixth largest <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">economy</a> in the world. It was a <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">superpower</a> during the 18th, 19th and early 20th century and was considered since the early 1800s to be the most powerful and influential nation in the world, in politics, economics (For it was the wealthiest country at the time.) and in military strength. Britain continued to be the biggest manufacturing economy in the world until 1908 and the largest economy until the 1920s. The economic cost of two world wars and the decline of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> in the 1950s and 1960s reduced its leading role in global affairs. The UK has strong economic, cultural, military and political influence and is a <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a>. It was a member state of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> until the UK left on February 1st, 2020. The UK holds a permanent seat on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>, and is a member of the <a href="/wiki/G8" title="G8">G8</a>, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, the capital, is famous as being the largest centre of <a href="/wiki/Finance" title="Finance">finance</a> in the world, along with <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=13" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Literature">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Change section: Literature">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <p><a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a> was an <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English</a> <a href="/wiki/Playwright" title="Playwright">playwright</a>. He wrote plays in the late 16th century. Some of his plays were <i><a href="/wiki/Romeo_and_Juliet" title="Romeo and Juliet">Romeo and Juliet</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Macbeth" title="Macbeth">Macbeth</a></i>. In the 19th century, <a href="/wiki/Jane_Austen" title="Jane Austen">Jane Austen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">Charles Dickens</a> were novelists. Twentieth century writers include the science fiction novelist <a href="/wiki/H.G._Wells" class="mw-redirect" title="H.G. Wells">H.G. Wells</a> and <a href="/wiki/J.R.R._Tolkien" class="mw-redirect" title="J.R.R. Tolkien">J.R.R. Tolkien</a>. The children's fantasy <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter" title="Harry Potter">Harry Potter</a></i> series was written by <a href="/wiki/J.K._Rowling" class="mw-redirect" title="J.K. Rowling">J.K. Rowling</a>. <a href="/wiki/Aldous_Huxley" title="Aldous Huxley">Aldous Huxley</a> was also from the United Kingdom. </p>
      <p>English language literature is written by authors from many countries. Eight people from the United Kingdom have won the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a>. <a href="/wiki/Seamus_Heaney" title="Seamus Heaney">Seamus Heaney</a> is a writer who was born in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Arthur_Conan_Doyle" title="Arthur Conan Doyle">Arthur Conan Doyle</a> from <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> wrote the <a href="/wiki/Sherlock_Holmes" title="Sherlock Holmes">Sherlock Holmes</a> detective novels. He was from <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>. The poet <a href="/wiki/Dylan_Thomas" title="Dylan Thomas">Dylan Thomas</a> brought Welsh culture to international attention. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=14" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Education">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Change section: Education">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="box-No_sources plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-4.svg" class="image"><img alt="Question book-4.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Question_book-4.svg/50px-Question_book-4.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Question_book-4.svg/75px-Question_book-4.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Question_book-4.svg/100px-Question_book-4.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="262" data-file-height="204"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>does not have any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> You can help Wikipedia by finding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:RELIABLE" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:RELIABLE">good</a> sources, and adding them.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2020</span>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>England, Northern Ireland, Scotland, and Wales have separate, but similar, systems of education. They all have rules that education is required from ages five to eighteen, except for in Scotland where school departure is allowed from the age of sixteen. Many children attend state schools and other children attend private schools. </p>
      <p>Britain's universities are the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a>, and London universities (<a href="/wiki/University_College_London" title="University College London">University College London</a>, the <a href="/wiki/London_School_of_Economics_and_Political_Science" class="mw-redirect" title="London School of Economics and Political Science">London School of Economics</a>, <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College_London" title="King's College London">King's College London</a> and <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College London</a>) which collectively form the Golden Triangle of UK universities. </p>
      <p>A broader group of twenty universities form the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Russell_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Russell Group (not yet started)">Russell Group</a>, which account for two thirds of research grants and contract funding out of the total of 100 universities. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=15" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Transport">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Change section: Transport">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="box-No_sources plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-4.svg" class="image"><img alt="Question book-4.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Question_book-4.svg/50px-Question_book-4.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Question_book-4.svg/75px-Question_book-4.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Question_book-4.svg/100px-Question_book-4.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="262" data-file-height="204"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>does not have any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> You can help Wikipedia by finding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:RELIABLE" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:RELIABLE">good</a> sources, and adding them.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2020</span>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Road traffic in the United Kingdom drives on the left hand side of the road (unlike the Americas and most of Europe), and the driver steers from the right hand side of the vehicle. The road network on the island of <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> is extensive, with most local and rural roads having evolved from Roman and Medieval times. Major routes developed in the mid 20th Century were made to the needs of the motor car. The high speed <a href="/wiki/Motorway" class="mw-redirect" title="Motorway">motorway</a> (freeway) network was mostly constructed in the 1960s and 1970s and links together major towns and cities. </p>
      <p>The system of <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport" title="Rail transport">rail transport</a> was invented in England and Wales, so the United Kingdom has the oldest <a href="/wiki/Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Railway">railway</a> network in the world. It was built mostly during the Victorian era. At the heart of the network are five long distance main lines which radiate from <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> to the major cities and secondary population centres with dense commuter networks within the regions. The newest part of the network connects London to the Channel Tunnel from St Pancras station and is built to the same standard as the French TGV system. The <a href="/wiki/British_Rail" title="British Rail">British Rail</a> network is part privatised, with privately owned train operating companies providing service along particular lines or regions, whilst the tracks, signals and stations are owned by a Government controlled company called Network Rail. In Northern Ireland the <a href="/wiki/NI_Railways" title="NI Railways">NI Railways</a> is the national railway. The system of underground railways in London, known as the <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">Tube</a>, has been copied by many other cities. </p>
      <p>Most domestic <a href="/wiki/Air_travel" title="Air travel">air travel</a> in the United Kingdom is between London and the major cities in Scotland and the North of England and <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>. <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow Airport">London-Heathrow</a> is the nation’s largest airport and is one of the most important international <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">hubs</a> in the world. Other major airports with principal international service include London-Gatwick, Birmingham, Manchester and Glasgow. </p>
      <p>An extensive system of <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">ferry</a> networks operate between the Scottish islands, and major ferry routes operate between England and France (via the English Channel), Scotland-Northern Ireland (via the Irish Sea) and England/Wales-Republic of Ireland (from Liverpool/Holyhead). </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=16" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Notes">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Change section: Notes">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

        <li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-3">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">There is no authorised version of the national anthem as the words are a matter of tradition; only the first verse is usually sung.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[1]</a></sup> No law was passed making "God Save the Queen" the official anthem.
